Domestic Important Telegrams Two

First Plenary Session

Yesterday's Three General Meetings

Passed the Organic Law of the National Government

Organizational Propaganda Changes to a Committee System

Recommended Chen Gongbo and Others to Draft a Declaration

The Meeting Will Adjourn Today and Resume Tomorrow

(Nanjing) The First Plenary Session held its third meeting at 8 a.m. on the 26th in the First Conference Hall of the Central Party Headquarters. The attending committee members were Huang Jichen, Yang Shukan, Shang Zhen, Deng Jiayan, Miao Peicheng, Xia Douyin, Zeng Kuangqing, Yu Youren, Zhu Peide, Huang Shi, Wu Tiecheng, Qian Dajun, Zhang Qun, Yang Jie, Zhang Zhiben, Xue Dubi, Li Ciwen, Zhu Jiahua, Pan Yunchao, He Yaozu, Jiao Yitang, Yang Hu, Wang Faqin, Zhu Jiqing, Wang Boling, Ding Chaowu, Ye Chucang, Huang Musong, Zhou Qigang, Fang Shengtao, He Yingqin, Zhang Dingfan, Gu Zhutong, Li Jingzhai, Zhang Weicun, Shao Yuanchong, Chen Lifu, Lin Yizhong, Miao Peinan, Qu Fangpu, Lin Sen, Li Zonghuang, Chen Gongbo, Dai Kuisheng, Fan Yusui, Duan Xipeng, Li Renren, Jing Hengyi, Chen Mingshu, Zheng Zhannan, Bai Yunti, Huang Shaogu, Gu Zhenggang, Yang Shuzhuang, Zhao Pilian, Zeng Yangfu, Zhang Daofan, Zou Lu, Wang Boqun, Cheng Qian, Li Liejun, Chen Zhaoying, Xiao Zhongzhen, Fang Zhenwu, Xiao Jishan, Liu Zhi, Deng Feihuang, Kong Xiangxi, Chen Guofu, Ma Chaojun, Zhang Lisheng, Wu Chaoshu, Wang Maogong, Mao Zuquan, Guo Chuntao, Ke Xing'e, Yu Jingtang, Chen Bijun, Gu Mengyu, Tang Youren, Hong Ludong, Wang Qi, Gan Naiguang, Huang Jilu, Xiong Kewu, Cui Guangxiu, Luo Jialun, Huang Fusheng, Shi Qingyang, Qin Zhen, Gui Chongji, Zeng Zhongming, Fang Juehui, Miao Bin, Shao Lizi, Xie Zuomin, Enke Batu, Ju Zheng, Guan Suren, Chen Zhongfu, etc., a total of one hundred people. Yu Youren served as chairman, Wu Tiecheng as secretary-general, and Zeng Zhongming as recorder. The following resolutions were passed:

(1) Passed the Organic Law of the National Government.

(2) Passed the standards for the election of the Chairman of the National Government, selecting and appointing those of high age and virtue.

(3) Regarding the proposal by Committee Member Gu Mengyu and others for party affairs reform, it was passed. The Central Organization Department and Propaganda Department were changed to the Organization Committee and Propaganda Committee. The Training Department was abolished, and a Mass Movement Guidance Committee was established instead.

(4) Committee Member He Xiangning and Committee Member Wang Qi proposed the implementation of a conscription system. The principle was approved, and the implementation period and methods were handed over to the National Government for proper planning.

(5) Committee Member Zhao Pilian proposed guaranteeing 1. active-duty military personnel and 2. service education personnel. Resolutions: 1. Passed and sent to the National Government to be handled properly by the competent authorities. 2. Sent to the National Government for reference.

(6) Recommended four committee members, Chen Gongbo, Ye Chucang, Deng Jiayan, and Luo Jialun, to draft a declaration for the plenary session. (Special dispatch on the 26th)

(Nanjing) Today's fourth plenary session of the conference, held as usual at 8:30 a.m., discussed an important telegram from Zhang Xueliang, detailing the Japanese army's threat to Jinzhou and the steadfast defense of the troops stationed there, and requesting final instructions on strategy and requesting supplies. The commissioners all felt that the case should be handled by the current National Government which had not yet been handed over. Then, the conference discussed the agenda. Due to Sun and Li's departure to Shanghai last night, and fewer commissioners arriving today, the voting scheduled for today and the agenda for tomorrow and the day after were all withdrawn and cancelled. The secretariat will organize and reissue them after referring to the facts. Therefore, the date for voting for the Chairman, Commissioners, and Presidents of the National Government could not be discussed today. As for foreign policy, it cannot be decided immediately, because all measures must be implemented, and before the government is formed, any resolutions submitted to the National Government for execution or review would be empty talk and not realistic. Therefore, the commissioners did not discuss foreign affairs or Wang's national salvation meeting in advance, but waited until the government was formed to vote and then hand it over to the new government to take responsibility for implementation. Therefore, the commissioners' energy at the meeting these days was not as high as in private negotiations regarding the selection of government personnel. (Special dispatch on the 26th)

(Nanjing) The term of the First Plenary Session was scheduled to end on the 26th, but the discussion of various proposals has not yet been completed, and the Chairman of the National Government and the President of the Executive Yuan have not yet been elected. It has been decided to extend the meeting by one day, and the fourth meeting will be held at noon on the 28th. After all matters are completed, a closing ceremony will be held immediately. (Special dispatch on the 26th)

(Nanjing) This afternoon, the general meeting continued. In addition to announcing five items, the presidium proposed a plan for the Premier's industrial plan and international cooperation to promote international peace and save the world economy, which was generally approved and handed over to Shao Yuanchong to organize the text. The conference will rest for one day on Sunday, the 27th. On the 28th, it is expected that the President of the National Government and the President of the Five Yuan will be voted on, and then the declaration of the conference will be published and the meeting will be closed. As for the candidate for the President of the National Government, there is now a saying that Yu Youren will be appointed. There is also a saying that Ju Zheng will be appointed as the President of the Examination Yuan. (Special dispatch on the 26th) (Nanjing) A certain commissioner said that although there will be a recess tomorrow, there will be substantive off-site consultations regarding the candidates for the President, Commissioners, and the President of the Executive Yuan. It was also discussed this evening that one of Cai and Lin will be elected as the President, and the other will be subsequently elected as the President of the Control Yuan. As for the President of the Executive Yuan, the commissioners from Nanjing all admire Wang, and the legislators favor Hu. The candidates for the various departments will be evaluated tomorrow to ensure a smooth outcome at the formal meeting on the 28th. Sun Ke will serve as the Vice President of the Executive Yuan and concurrently as the Minister of Finance. It is also planned to assign Zou Lu and Ju Zheng to the positions of Minister and Vice President. (Special dispatch on the 26th) (Nanjing) At the three general meetings today, there was a discussion on the Jinzhou issue. The content was not disclosed due to foreign affairs considerations. (Special dispatch on the 26th)

(Nanjing) Ten Central Commissioners, including Cai Yuanpei, Yu Youren, He Yingqin, Zhu Peide, Shao Yuanchong, and Shao Lizi, are scheduled to host a banquet for all the Central Commissioners at the Lizhi Society at 7 p.m. on the 27th. (Special dispatch on the 26th)

Feng Yuxiang

Goes South with Liu Shouchong

To Attend the First Plenary Session

Yan's Date of Departure Is Undecided

(Taiyuan) Feng Yuxiang, along with Liu Shouchong and Yang Aiyuan, took a Zhengtai special train at 6:30 a.m. on the 26th to Shijiazhuang, and then took the Jinpu Railway to Jinjing (Nanjing) to attend the plenary session. Yan is still at home. It is undecided whether Zhao Daiwen will go to Beijing. On the evening of the 25th, Feng telegraphed Jiang, Zhang, Wang, and Hu to report the date of departure. (Special dispatch on the 26th)

(Tianjin) Feng Yuxiang arrived in Shijiazhuang at noon on the 26th. The Jinpu Railway had already prepared a special train to pick him up and take him south. (Special dispatch on the 26th)

(Taiyuan) Feng Yuxiang and Liu Shouchong left Bing (Taiyuan) at 6 a.m. on the 26th. Yang Aiyuan did not go. According to his entourage, Feng will go directly to Beijing from Tianjin, and will return to Shanxi after the meeting. Zhao Daiwen told reporters that Yan originally planned to come to Bing after Wang and Hu replied to their telegram, and discuss together. Now that Feng and Liu have left, Yan will not come for the time being. Yan is indeed planning to go to Beijing, but the date of departure is undecided. He is extremely concerned about national affairs and intends to go to Beijing, but his poor health makes it difficult to fulfill his wish. He hopes that all parties will work together to overcome the difficulties, abolish the Guangdong government as soon as possible, establish a unified government quickly, and unanimously confront foreign enemies. (Special dispatch on the 26th)

(Taiyuan) Feng Yuxiang decided to go to Beijing on the morning of the 26th with Liu Shouchong and Yang Aiyuan, two Central Commissioners. Before his departure, he sent a telegram to the Fourth Session of the First Plenary Session, which read: "To the Plenary Meeting of the Fourth Central Executive and Supervisory Committee of the Chinese Kuomintang in Nanjing: I have repeatedly received telegrams from your meeting and Comrades Hu, Lin, and Sun urging me to go to Beijing to attend. With the country in distress, how dare I indulge myself? I have decided to leave Bing on the morning of the 26th, take the road via Shijiazhuang and Fengtai, and transfer to the Jinpu Railway south. Respectfully reported, Feng Yuxiang, etc." He also sent a telegram to Zhang Xueliang, which read: "To Commander Zhang, Hanqing, my dear brother: I recently heard that the Japanese army has launched a major offensive against Jinzhou, and our army is fighting fiercely. With such foreign troubles, there is no time to waste. I have repeatedly received telegrams from the Fourth Plenary Session and Comrades Wang, Sun, Hu, and Lin urging me to go to Beijing to attend and jointly address the national crisis. I have decided to leave Bing at 6 a.m. on the 26th, transfer to the Pinghan Railway via Shijiazhuang and Fengtai, then transfer to the Beining Railway to Tianjin, and then transfer to the Jinpu Railway south to Beijing. Respectfully reported, Feng Yuxiang, etc." In addition, he sent telegrams to Han Fuju and others, and telegraphed Xue Dubi in Beijing to prepare accommodation. (Special dispatch on the 25th) (Beiping) Zhang Xueliang sent a representative to Shijiazhuang to welcome Feng Yuxiang and prepared a special train for Feng to take to Beijing. (Special dispatch on the 26th)

Disputes During the Second General Meeting

The Process of Verbal Disputes

Chen and Zou Come to Shanghai to Urge Sun to Return to Beijing

Wu Jingheng Is Willing to Accept Warnings

But Claims He Will Not Change His Views

(Nanjing) According to Wu Jingheng's own account, his speech yesterday was his personal opinion and did not represent the overall opinion of the Beijing side. He has not changed his views so far. If the meeting wants to warn him, he will accept it, but he hopes that the meeting will not only attack the Beijing side, then he will not demand that those who sold out the country by colluding with Japan be held responsible. Because the resolutions of the Shanghai meeting were a compromise of mutual concessions, not a conquest of the Beijing side, and not a public trial of the Beijing Commissioners. If only the Beijing side is held responsible, it would be very unfair. (Special dispatch on the 26th)

(Nanjing) The situation of the discussion and disputes in yesterday's meeting was reported in brief yesterday and can be seen in today's newspaper. Today, a certain committee member, who was involved in the matter, talked about the truth at the time, which was even more thorough than the rumors. He said that yesterday, a certain Guangdong commissioner proposed a motion to punish Zhang Xueliang, speaking eloquently and incessantly, saying that not only should Zhang be held responsible for losing the battle and losing territory, but the Nanjing government should also bear major responsibility. After the report, Wu Jingheng immediately stood up and said that Zhang Xueliang should be responsible, and the Nanjing government should also be responsible for non-resistance, and those who went to Japan to collude with Japan to bring disaster to China must also be held responsible. A certain Guangdong commissioner stood up and questioned what Wu meant by "those who sold out the country." Wu replied that those involved should know. At that time, some people shouted "right, right, right," and others shouted "tsk, tsk, tsk." This is one incident. Also, in the amendment to the Organic Law of the National Government, Wu also stood up to express his opinion, saying that the President of the Executive Yuan is the de facto responsible cabinet, and the standard for selecting the person should be someone with methods. If he only seeks vain reputation and has no methods, then changing the system will not help in practice. We must not blindly follow suit. Please pay attention. The Guangdong commissioners felt that Wu's words seemed to have some implications, and they were even more dissatisfied. Therefore, some people suggested that Sun Ke, Li Wenfan, and Fu Bingchang should leave first to show their coldness, and demanded that Wu be warned not to make such remarks that would undermine cooperation in the future, so as to create room for maneuver. (Special dispatch on the 26th)

(Nanjing) After today's meeting, regarding Sun Ke and others' departure to Shanghai, one side blamed Wu Jingheng for talking too much, and the other side blamed Sun Ke for being rash, saying that it was contrary to the spirit of cooperation originally agreed upon at the peace conference. It was decided to send Chen Mingshu and Zou Lu to Shanghai to persuade Sun to return as soon as possible. On the one hand, a certain commissioner from the Beijing side admitted to persuading Wu Jingheng not to attend the next meeting, and it is expected that Sun Ke can return, because in recent off-site negotiations, the facts of various issues are not very different from Sun's expectations. Sun should not give up this accomplished situation. (Special dispatch on the 26th)

(Nanjing) Sun Ke, Li Wenfan, and other commissioners suddenly left Beijing for Shanghai. Chen Mingshu and Zou Lu took a fast train to Shanghai at noon on the 26th to report to Sun, Li, and others that everyone hopes to return to the capital as soon as possible to discuss important matters together. Chen and Zou will take this opportunity to inquire about Wang Jingwei's condition and urge the commissioners Li Jishen and Li Zongren, who recently came to Shanghai from Guangdong, to go to Beijing as soon as possible. Chen and Zou are scheduled to return to Beijing on the 27th. (Special dispatch on the 26th)

(Nanjing) Chen Mingshu went to Shanghai in the afternoon of the 26th to contact Wang, Sun, and other Central Commissioners in Shanghai and urged them to go to Beijing to attend the meeting. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 26th)

(Nanjing) He Yingqin said that Wu and Sun had verbal disputes, and Sun Zhesheng and Li Junpei had gone to Shanghai. Jiang Zuobin went to Shanghai that night to welcome and persuade them. I think Sun and Li will definitely value the ardent hope of the colleagues at the conference and will not disregard the national crisis due to trivial matters. (Special dispatch on the 26th)

(Nanjing) After Central Commissioner Sun Ke took a train to Shanghai on the evening of the 25th, the First Plenary Session successively sent personnel to Shanghai to welcome him. It is now heard that Sun has decided to take a night train from Shanghai to Beijing on the 27th to attend the fourth general meeting of the plenary session so as to participate in the election of the President of the National Government and the presidents of the five Yuan. (Special dispatch on the 26th)

Northeastern Fellow Townsmen

Petition the First Plenary Session

(Nanjing) Northeastern fellow townsmen residing in Beijing, including Li Menggeng, Feng Jiyi, Wang Xingzhou, and Li Shiyong, petitioned the plenary session on the 26th. The presidium sent personnel to meet them and fully accepted the points of the petition. The points of the petition of Li and others were: (1) to send troops to reinforce Jinzhou as soon as possible and then recover the lost territory; (2) to urge the leaders to unite sincerely and jointly face the national crisis; (3) to provide practical assistance in terms of personnel and resources; (4) to implement revolutionary diplomacy; (5) to settle the Northeastern students who have lost their schools. (Special dispatch on the 26th)

Two Proposals in the General Meeting

Transferred to the Standing Committee for Research

(Nanjing) The proposal to establish political sub-committees in the North, Guangzhou, and Wuhan was discussed at the second general meeting on the 24th. The commissioners believed that this proposal was greatly related to the future political organization of our country and could not be considered for a long time, and it was decided to transfer it to the Standing Committee for meticulous research and implementation after drafting an outline. (Special dispatch on the 26th)

Foreign Telegrams

Czech Representative to Russia

Conspired to Assassinate Hirota

Aimed to Incite a Russo-Japanese War

Warnerck Recalled to Prague

Prague, 26th National News Agency Dispatch: The Associated Press learned today that Warnerck, the secretary of the Czechoslovakian representative in Russia, was in fact instructed by Soviet Russia to conspire to assassinate the Japanese ambassador and demand the withdrawal of diplomatic personnel from the country. Mr. Warnerck is only 35 years old and is known as a military expert among several major European powers. The Soviet Secret Police accused him of plotting to incite Russians to assassinate Japanese Ambassador Hirota in an attempt to escalate the Sino-Japanese Liaoning Incident into a Russo-Japanese war. Mr. Warnerck has now been recalled to Prague at the request of the Russian government. However, the Czech authorities still deny this, claiming that Mr. Warnerck was recalled due to illness. However, according to the Associated Press, Mr. Warnerck was indeed recalled at the request of Soviet Russia and has already departed from Moscow and is expected to arrive in Prague on Monday. According to sources in Moscow, when Russian diplomats reported Warnerck's conspiracy to the Czech representative in Russia, Mr. Guo Xianke, Mr. Guo initially did not believe it, saying that none of his staff would be able to hide their private political actions from him. However, Mr. Guo then agreed to send Warnerck back to his country immediately. On Friday, Mr. Guo telephoned the Japanese Embassy and informed them that Warnerck had left for Prague due to illness. However, it is heard that Mr. Warnerck actually left Moscow today. Although Czechoslovakia has not formally recognized Soviet Russia, it has sent a diplomatic representative to Moscow, who enjoys full diplomatic privileges. However, its representatives are often chosen outside of political considerations. Therefore, when correspondents from Moscow newspapers heard about this conspiracy, although they speculated about the mastermind, few expected it to be within the Czech delegation.

Tokyo, 26th National News Agency Dispatch: The Japanese government has now clearly stated that the discovery of the conspiracy to assassinate Japanese Ambassador Hirota in Moscow should not cause international disputes, and declared that the incident has been resolved locally in Moscow. The Japanese government therefore intends to express its gratitude to the Soviet Russian police for this matter. According to reports, the conspiracy was hatched by a certain embassy official, Mr. A, who planned to shoot the Japanese ambassador in order to provoke a war between Japan and Russia. The embassy official also discussed this matter with a close friend, a Russian, Mr. B, and strongly encouraged him to take on the task. Mr. B then reported the information to the police. Furthermore, a telegram from the Czech capital stated that a certain official of the Czech diplomatic mission in Moscow has now been recalled by his country, presumably in connection with this matter.

Philippines

Restricting Immigration

Chinese Most Affected

Manila, 26th Reuters Dispatch: The Philippine government will reduce the number of ports of entry for foreigners in order to prevent them from entering the country illegally, which will affect the Chinese the most. Acting Governor Butter has ordered an investigation into the illegal entry of Chinese into the Philippine Islands. Two cabinet members have gone south to conduct this investigation, as many Chinese enter through ports in the south. The cabinet members have discussed two methods to deal with this matter: one is to reduce the number of ports of entry for immigrants, and in the future, only Manila will be the legal port of entry; the other is to establish special investigation bureaus at all ports of entry for foreigners to strictly monitor foreigners entering the country. The Chinese Consul General in Manila is now willing to cooperate with the Philippine government to reduce the number of Chinese who illegally enter the Philippines by starting with an investigation of the household registration of overseas Chinese on various islands. Qualified overseas residents will be issued special certificates. This cooperation has been welcomed by the Philippine immigration authorities.

60th

Japanese Parliament Opens Yesterday

Emperor Personally Delivers Address

Dissolution Inevitable

Tokyo, 26th National News Agency Dispatch: The 60th session of the Diet officially opened at 11:00 this morning. The Emperor, wearing the uniform of the Grand Marshal, attended the House of Peers and delivered an address. Members of both houses arrived one after another at 9:00 AM. The Emperor was greeted by Prime Minister Inukai Tsuyoshi and his cabinet members. The meeting adjourned at 11:10 AM and will reconvene on January 21st of next year. At that time, Prime Minister Inukai Tsuyoshi, Finance Minister Takahashi, and Acting Foreign Minister Inukai Tsuyoshi will deliver speeches outlining the Seiyukai's policies on finance and the Manchurian situation. Inukai Tsuyoshi will also outline the government's administrative policies for the Diet. It is expected that the Diet will be dissolved after the speeches, and a general election will be held around the end of February.

Closing of the Russian Central Executive Committee

Approved Various Figures

Economy to Overwhelm the World

No Illiterates in Russia in Five Years

Stalin's Bold Statement

Moscow, 26th Havas Dispatch: The Soviet Central Executive Committee held its final meeting. Chairman Molotov of the Council of People's Commissars delivered a closing speech. The audience listened attentively. The gist was that the various figures for 1932, after being verified by the supervisory authorities and submitted to the Council of People's Commissars, have been approved by the Executive Committee. This shows that the economic construction plan for next year has been formally established, and the hydroelectric power plant under construction has historical value. Molotov then described the most important factories that should be opened next year, especially the Gugerske Factory, the Manitogorsk Factory, the Glisalok Factory, and the Svie Power Plant. The Soviet government intends to make every effort to improve the food supply for the working class. Ninety-two food factories will begin operations, including 18 flour mills, 12 meat processing plants, 2 refineries (sugar and kerosene), and 23 canneries. Molotov concluded by saying that the Soviet people have the full will to implement the Five-Year Plan. We do not need to discuss foreign policy much, because the Soviet government's peace policy and its actions based on this policy are very obvious and do not need explanation. Molotov also compared the funds needed by the United States to relieve the panic with the situation of the Soviet economic recovery, and said that the Soviet social organization is extremely great, and rumors from outside are therefore spreading. We can ignore this kind of instigation, but we only seek to complete the 1932 plan and pay close attention to ensuring that our claims can overcome everything. After Molotov's speech, Cherjingyakov, Chairman of the Central Executive Committee of the Byelorussian Soviet Socialist Republic, presented a resolution approving the domestic and foreign affairs of the Soviet Union and the various figures for 1932 after being verified by the supervisory authorities, which was unanimously passed.

Moscow News: The most noteworthy event at the recent plenary session of the Soviet Russian Central Executive Committee was the report on economic development. Chairman Stalin delivered his proud oratory, claiming that after the success of the Five-Year Plan, Soviet Russia would definitely be able to overwhelm capitalist countries around the world economically. The results of the Five-Year Plan reported at the conference are as follows: (1) In the past four years, the cultivated land has increased from 1,522,500 acres to 2,500,000 acres, and will increase to 3,100,000 acres next year. (2) The most rapid development in industry is timber and fishery products. The current Soviet Russian timber and fisheries industry has surpassed any country in the world. (3) The cultural development of uncivilized areas in border regions is also quite impressive. According to this year's survey, the number of illiterate people has decreased by more than 35% compared to before the European War. In the next five years, there will be no one illiterate in the entire Russian territory. (World News Agency)

Christmas Eve Gloom

Paris Unemployed Workers Demonstrate

Chilean Communists Attack Barracks

Paris, 25th Havas Dispatch: Christmas Eve suppers were slightly subdued due to the impact of the economic panic. Although restaurants reduced prices and dishes, there were fewer customers than in previous years. The weather was cold that day, with rain and snow at night. The midnight Mass in churches was very crowded, and the theaters were also full. The Latin Quarter and Montparnasse, belonging to the academic and artistic circles, were especially lively. The Montmartre entertainment district only began celebrating at midnight, following the old traditions. Organizations for the poor's suppers increased as a result of the economic panic compared to previous years. Thousands of beggars were provided with food by the Salvation Army, and Boy Scouts distributed meat, bread, and soup at the door, so there were many disappointed people. The newspapers belonging to the Communist Party called on unemployed workers to demonstrate in front of various supper restaurants. Nine unemployed workers demonstrating in Montmartre were carrying military equipment and were arrested by the police. There were also demonstrations by unemployed workers near the Presidential Palace and Montparnasse.

Santiago, Chile, 25th National News Agency Dispatch: On Christmas Day, the barracks in Copiapó, Chile, were attacked by 300 communists. One officer, two soldiers, and eight civilians were killed in the attack, including two female communist members. They were all workers from nitrate plants near Copiapó. At the time of the riot, a large part of the officers stationed in the city were on Christmas leave, which was taken advantage of by the rioters. However, after a fierce counterattack, the garrison regained the barracks.

US Police Discover

Plot to Harm Mr. Stimson

Heavy Guard Around Residence

Washington, 25th National News Agency Dispatch: The Washington police authorities recently received a report that someone was plotting to harm Secretary of State Stimson. Therefore, starting today, there has been a heavy guard around Mr. Stimson's residence. The police authorities have not announced the content of the plot to harm the Secretary of State, nor are they willing to say the source of the information. However, after obtaining the information, they consulted with Mr. Stimson and obtained his permission to add guards around his residence. The State Department said that Mr. Stimson himself had not received any threatening letters, nor had he requested police protection. The police are currently actively investigating and it is expected that arrests will be made soon.
