Important News

First Plenary Session of the Central Committee Revises

The Organic Law of the National Government

Passed at the Third Meeting

The revised Organic Law of the National Government of the Republic of China was passed at the third meeting of the Fourth Plenary Session of the First Central Committee on the 26th. The full text is recorded below.

Chapter I: General Provisions (Article 1) The National

Government formulates the Organic Law of the National Government of the Republic of China in accordance with Article 77 of the Provisional Constitution for the Period of Political Tutelage of the Republic of China.

Chapter II: The National Government (Article 2) The National

Government oversees the governing power of the Republic of China. (Article 3) The National Government commands the army, navy, and air force. (Article 4) The National Government exercises the power to declare war, make peace, and conclude treaties. (Article 5) The National Government promulgates laws and issues orders. (Article 6) The National Government grants amnesties, pardons, and reduces or restores sentences. (Article 7) The National Government confers honors. (Article 8) The National Government independently exercises the five powers of governance: administration, legislation, judiciary, examination, and supervision through the following five yuan: 1. Executive Yuan, 2. Legislative Yuan, 3. Judicial Yuan, 4. Examination Yuan, 5. Control Yuan. Each of the aforementioned Yuan may promulgate orders in accordance with the law. (Article 9) The National Government may establish directly subordinate agencies when necessary, which are directly subordinate to the National Government, and their organization shall be determined by law. (Article 10) The National Government shall have one Chairman and twenty-four to thirty-six Members. Each Yuan shall have a President and Vice-President, who shall be elected by the Central Executive Committee of the Kuomintang. (Article 11) The Chairman of the National Government is the Head of State of the Republic of China and represents the National Government internally and externally, but does not bear actual political responsibility. (Article 12) The Chairman of the National Government may not hold any other official positions. (Article 13) The Chairman of the National Government shall hold office for a term of two years and may be re-elected once, but shall be re-elected in accordance with the law when the Constitution is promulgated. (Article 14) All orders and dispositions of the National Government, as well as orders concerning military mobilization, shall be signed by the Chairman of the National Government, but shall only take effect after being signed by the President or Minister of the Yuan concerned. (Article 15) Before the promulgation of the Constitution, the Executive, Legislative, Judicial, Control, and Examination Yuan shall each be responsible to the Central Executive Committee of the Kuomintang.

Page 9

Continued Important News

Chapter III: National Government Committee (Article 16)

The National Government Committee is composed of the Chairman and Members of the National Government. (Article 17) Matters that cannot be resolved between Yuan shall be decided by the National Government Committee. (Article 18) The Rules of Procedure for the National Government Committee meeting shall be determined separately.

Chapter IV: Executive Yuan (Article 19) The Executive Yuan is

the highest administrative organ of the National Government. (Article 20) The Executive Yuan shall establish various Ministries to administer administrative functions. Committees may be established to manage specific administrative matters. (Article 21) Each Ministry of the Executive Yuan shall have one Minister, one Political Vice-Minister, and one Administrative Vice-Minister. Each Committee shall have one Chairman, one Vice-Chairman, and a number of Members. The candidates for Minister and Chairman of each Ministry of the Executive Yuan shall be nominated by the President of the Executive Yuan and appointed and dismissed by the Chairman of the National Government in accordance with the law. The Political Vice-Ministers, Administrative Vice-Ministers of each Ministry, and the Vice-Chairmen and Members of each Committee shall be nominated by the President of the Executive Yuan and appointed and dismissed by the Chairman of the National Government in accordance with the law. (Article 22) If the President of the Executive Yuan is unable to perform his duties due to an accident, the Vice-President shall act as his agent. (Article 23) The Executive Yuan meeting shall be composed of the President, Vice-President, Ministers of each Ministry, and Chairmen of each Committee of the Executive Yuan. The President of the Executive Yuan shall chair the meeting. (Article 24) The following matters shall be decided by the Executive Yuan meeting: (1) Legal bills submitted to the Legislative Yuan; (2) Budget bills submitted to the Legislative Yuan; (3) Amnesty bills submitted to the Legislative Yuan; (4) Declarations of war and peace treaties submitted to the Legislative Yuan; (5) Appointment and dismissal of administrative and judicial officials above the level of Recommended Appointment; (6) Matters that cannot be resolved between various Ministries and Committees of the Executive Yuan; (7) Other matters that are required by law or that the President of the Executive Yuan deems should be submitted to the Executive Yuan meeting for decision. (Article 25) All orders and dispositions of the Executive Yuan shall only take effect after being countersigned by all the Ministers for general administrative matters, and by the Ministers of the relevant Ministries for local administrative matters. (Article 26) The organization of the Executive Yuan shall be determined by law.

Chapter V: Legislative Yuan (Article 27) The Legislative Yuan

is the highest legislative organ of the National Government. The Legislative Yuan has the power to deliberate on legal bills, budget bills, amnesty bills, declarations of war, peace treaties, and other important international matters. (Article 28) If the President of the Legislative Yuan is unable to perform his duties due to an accident, the Vice-President shall act as his agent. (Article 29) The Presidents of each Yuan and the Heads of each Ministry and Committee of the Executive Yuan may attend Legislative Yuan meetings to provide explanations. (Article 30) The Legislative Yuan shall establish fifty to one hundred Legislative Members, who shall be nominated by the President of the Legislative Yuan and appointed by the Chairman of the National Government in accordance with the law. Half of the aforementioned members shall be elected by legal people's organizations, and the election law shall be determined separately. (Article 31) Legislative Members shall hold office for a term of two years, but may be re-elected. (Article 32) Legislative Members may not hold any other official positions. (Article 33) The President of the Legislative Yuan shall chair the Legislative Yuan meeting. (Article 34) The organization of the Legislative Yuan shall be determined by law.

Chapter VI: Judicial Yuan (Article 35) The Judicial Yuan

is the highest judicial organ of the National Government. Matters concerning special pardons, sentence reductions, and restoration of rights shall be submitted by the President of the Judicial Yuan to the Chairman of the National Government for signature in accordance with the law. (Article 36) The Judicial Yuan shall establish a Supreme Court, an Administrative Court, and a Commission on Disciplinary Sanctions for Public Functionaries. (Article 37) The President of the Judicial Yuan shall concurrently serve as the President of the Supreme Court, and the Vice-President of the Judicial Yuan shall concurrently serve as the Chairman of the Commission on Disciplinary Sanctions for Public Functionaries. (Article 38) The President of the Judicial Yuan may attend and hear the trials of the Administrative Court and the Commission on Disciplinary Sanctions for Public Functionaries when he deems it necessary. (Article 39) If the President of the Judicial Yuan is unable to perform his duties due to an accident, the Vice-President shall act as his agent. (Article 40) The Judicial Yuan may submit proposals to the Legislative Yuan regarding matters under its jurisdiction. (Article 41) The organization of the Judicial Yuan shall be determined by law.

Chapter VII: Examination Yuan (Article 42) The Examination Yuan

is the highest examination organ of the National Government, and shall exercise the functions of examination and appointment in accordance with the law. (Article 43) If the President of the Examination Yuan is unable to perform his duties due to an accident, the Vice-President shall act as his agent. (Article 44) The Examination Yuan may submit proposals to the Legislative Yuan regarding matters under its jurisdiction. (Article 45) The organization of the Examination Yuan shall be determined by law.

Chapter VIII: Control Yuan (Article 46) The Control Yuan

is the highest supervisory organ of the National Government, and shall exercise the functions of impeachment and auditing in accordance with the law. (Article 47) If the President of the Control Yuan is unable to perform his duties due to an accident, the Vice-President shall act as his agent. (Article 48) The Control Yuan shall establish thirty to fifty Control Members, who shall be nominated by the President of the Control Yuan and appointed by the Chairman of the National Government in accordance with the law. Half of the aforementioned members shall be elected by legal people's organizations, and the election law shall be determined separately. (Article 49) The protection of Control Members shall be determined by law. (Article 50) The Control Yuan meeting shall be composed of Control Members, and the President of the Control Yuan shall be the Chairman of the Control Yuan meeting. (Article 51) Control Members may not hold other public offices concurrently. (Article 52) The Control Yuan may submit proposals to the Legislative Yuan regarding matters under its jurisdiction. (Article 53) The organization of the Control Yuan shall be determined by law.

Chapter IX: Supplementary Provisions (Article 54) This law shall be implemented from the date of

promulgation.

Foreign Reports

Japanese Army Ceases Attack on Jinzhou

Shenyang, 25th, Da Mei Evening News: Whether General Honjo of the Japanese Army's second military operation west of the South Manchurian Railway Line intends to attack Jinzhou or merely suppress bandits is unknown to outsiders. However, the operation appears to have been abruptly halted. The suddenness and strangeness of the halt is no different from the sudden withdrawal of troops advancing towards Jinzhou in November. The true situation at this time is still unclear, but the so-called bandit suppression military operation west of the South Manchurian Railway and north of Shenyang, which was launched with a mixed brigade and three large battalions, only found 300 of those designated as irregular troops, killed 100 of them, and then stopped abruptly. Prior to this, the Japanese Army Headquarters claimed that there were 15,000 soldiers and bandits in the area, endangering Japanese communication lines. As for the troops sent to the area south of Shenyang and west of the South Manchurian Railway, it is now announced that they have actually all returned to their bases. The only result of this action is the occupation of the towns of Tianzhuangtai and Niuzhuang. The Japanese Army Headquarters is still silent about the battle of Tianzhuangtai. However, according to reports here, Japanese troops set out from Yingkou and crossed the Liao River on the second day. They were actually surrounded by Chinese troops, who used artillery to break the ice on the Liao River to prevent the Japanese from sending reinforcements. After a long time, the Japanese army brought in artillery, and used artillery fire to force the Chinese artillery to retreat, so that they could send troops across the river to reinforce the besieged Japanese soldiers. Later, Japanese armored vehicles advanced to the northwest and encountered Chinese armored vehicles. The Chinese armored vehicles had two field guns, so they opened fire on each other. However, the Chinese army eventually retreated towards Dawa due to its isolated position. The Japanese army occupied Tianzhuangtai, and then advanced further, but at this time they received an order to retreat. As for the Japanese military communique here, it only stated that the Chinese soldiers suffered heavy casualties, without saying anything else. Furthermore, it is reliably reported tonight that the Japanese army has stopped advancing and is currently scouting the location of what they call bandits and irregular troops. When reporters asked whether General Honjo considered the engagement of Chinese regular troops on the Yingkou Line a pretext to start an attack on Jinzhou, the spokesman for the Japanese Army Headquarters avoided answering and only described various bandit alarms in detail.

Current Situation in Heilongjiang

Suzuki Brigade Dispatched to Liaoning

Atrocities of Japanese Troops in the City

Harbin Dispatch, Qiqihar News: On November 19th, Japanese troops, the Second Division led by General Tamon, consisting of approximately 3,000 infantry, cavalry, and artillery, entered the city. On November 28th, the said division withdrew from Heilongjiang, leaving only the Nagatani Brigade stationed, numbering approximately two to three hundred. On December 2nd, the Suzuki Tsūmi Division arrived in Heilongjiang, numbering approximately one thousand. Subsequently, the majority of them withdrew the day before yesterday. Currently, the Japanese troops stationed in Heilongjiang number no more than five to six hundred, including the aviation unit. The locations where Japanese troops are currently stationed are as follows: the aviation unit is stationed at the Jiaotong Middle School and Normal School, and the airfield (under construction since November 25th) is west of the Normal School, only about two li away from the provincial capital, with a strength of no more than one hundred. The communication unit is stationed at the First Primary School in front of the Chamber of Commerce. The military police are stationed in the front courtyard of the clothing factory. The cavalry is stationed at the Jiangwutang, numbering less than two hundred and fifty. The artillery is stationed at the Longjiang Station, numbering less than one hundred. Other infantry are scattered in the Japanese Consulate, the South Manchuria Railway Company office, and the South Barracks, appearing intermittently. The headquarters is located inside the South Manchuria Railway Company office. The actual strength of the Japanese troops includes six aircraft, only one of which is a monoplane, two armored vehicles, one searchlight vehicle, no more than ten flat-trajectory guns, an unspecified number of machine guns, and several military vehicles. Tanks have not been seen.

Japanese aircraft fly daily from 9:00 AM to 12:00 PM, dropping bombs as a show of force along the river and occasionally strafing with machine guns, claiming it is practice. The infantry, cavalry, and artillery sometimes parade in formation and sometimes conduct live-fire exercises in the suburbs. In short, although their numbers are not large, they make a show of strength by marching through the streets and alleys to intimidate our people. During this time of frantic activity, the Japanese troops also take time for inspections. Those inspected include the residence of Zhai Xiren, the Zhang residence (the home of Wan's father-in-law), and the Zhang Mingjiu residence, which were inspected twice. The first inspection took place on November 24th, and the second on the 6th of this month. The first inspection yielded nothing. The second inspection found five hundred rounds of ammunition, four machine guns, and more than twenty rifles. It is also rumored that unauthorized Japanese soldiers have broken into other civilian residences. Since the Japanese troops entered the city, bandits have sprung up in the countryside, and many villagers have come to the city to avoid the bandit threat. However, they know that the city is also disturbed several times a night, so they can only reside temporarily after entering the city. The order in the city is maintained by the Public Security Bureau and the Special Zone Garrison, so it is still considered relatively peaceful. The merchants have gradually resumed business since the day after the Japanese troops entered the city. The Japanese troops, fearing the cold, often suffer from chapped hands and cracked feet. A certain photo studio has photos of Japanese soldiers' frozen hands and feet. According to the studio, there are a total of fourteen types, with eight prints of each type being developed for mailing to Japan. These photos were taken the day after the Japanese troops occupied Heilongjiang. According to the Japanese, the frostbite occurred during the fighting with the Heilongjiang army in Daxing. The chapped hands and cracked feet in the photos are truly unsightly, with the diameter of the frozen fingers and toes being about one inch. It can be seen that the Japanese troops are not able to withstand the cold. Furthermore, the Japanese troops, hearing rumors of a counterattack by Ma Zhanshan, are constantly on guard. At night, sentries are stationed at the South Manchuria Railway Company office and other places. Whenever General Ma is mentioned, they cannot help but turn pale.

Someone who returned from Heilongjiang yesterday said that the Japanese troops recently conducted a very thorough search of various merchants in Heilongjiang Province. Those who have military supplies will immediately be accused of collaborating with the enemy and their officers will be arrested. A certain military clothing store on West Street had two thousand sets of gray military uniforms in stock, which were made for a certain brigade before the Heilongjiang Incident but had not been taken away before the retreat. The Japanese troops found them, poured kerosene on them in the street, and burned them. The storefronts of nearby stores were mostly damaged by the flames. Because the Japanese troops were monitoring the scene, even those who were affected dared not try to put out the fire with all their might, so three or four families were implicated. The shopkeeper of the military clothing store was taken away and has not yet been released. It is also said that the Longjiang Hotel, the largest in Heilongjiang, has been searched under the pretext that Chinese military officers resided in the hotel. However, they did not find anything. The evening before last (the 16th), three Japanese and two Chinese who were pro-Japanese led more than ten Japanese military police to occupy the hotel. Because the owner, Li Zhendong, was not in Harbin, the Japanese arrested the clerks Yang Ruifeng, Liu Jinglin, and Le Zhenzhi and took them to the Japanese military police headquarters. It is heard that Li Zhendong believes that the hotel is self-operated by merchants, and it is not known on what basis the Japanese forcibly took over it. Yesterday, a petition document was drafted in Harbin, requesting the Heilongjiang local maintenance association to negotiate with the Japanese side. (Evening of the 19th)

Zang Shiyi's Acceptance of a Puppet Position

Harbin Dispatch: After Puyi was abducted to Shenyang by Itagaki, the "Manchu-Mongol Puppet Dynasty" was not immediately realized due to the Japanese government's uncertain policy. The intention of the Minister of the Army, Minami, was to disregard everything and immediately establish a Manchu-Mongol Political Committee, with personnel from the Army, Foreign Affairs, and Colonial Affairs Ministries, as well as the president of the South Manchuria Railway Company and the commander of the Kwantung Army, as the core personnel to carry out governance. However, Foreign Minister Shidehara, considering diplomatic issues, was not quite convinced and advocated for a gradual approach, first supporting a puppet to the stage, with Japan avoiding direct control and then annexing it after some years. This plan was the focus of debate between the military and diplomatic factions in the Japanese government before the previous cabinet collapsed, and it remained unresolved. Although the recent reorganization of the Japanese cabinet was caused by the military faction's criticism of the previous cabinet's weak policy towards China, the plan to establish a new Manchu-Mongol regime seems to have not changed. The Japanese still want to use a puppet as a transition before annexation. However, looking around among the Chinese traitors in Shenyang, people like Yuan Jinkai were not enough to rally everyone. After much hesitation, they turned their attention to Zang Shiyi, the former chairman. On the 15th of this month, hundreds of representatives from commercial and industrial groups in Shenyang, under the command of Japanese military personnel, held a meeting at the Chamber of Commerce and Industry, resolving to ask the local maintenance committee to voluntarily disband and publicly nominate Zang Shiyi as the governor of the province to organize a formal government. After the meeting, the Japanese military police forced each merchant and civilian family to send one person, holding banners with the words "The gentry, merchants, farmers, and workers of the entire Fengtian city publicly support Zang Gong as the ninth governor of the province" and other words, led by Yuan Jinkai and others to Zang's residence to persuade him to take office. Zang was initially hesitant, but after much persuasion, he reluctantly agreed. On the afternoon of the 16th, the local maintenance committee held a ceremony in the provincial governor's office to hand over power. Yuan Jinkai gave a speech, and Zang Shiyi responded. From the 18th, Zang began to work in the puppet provincial office, with several Japanese advisors accompanying him in and out to secretly monitor him. Zang also set the office hours from 10:00 AM to 12:00 PM and from 2:30 PM to 4:00 PM, and the visiting hours from 12:00 PM to 2:30 PM. Currently, all personnel from the old maintenance committee have been dismissed. Yuan Jinkai has been hired as an advisor to the puppet provincial office. Weng En-yu, who was the Director of Finance in the maintenance committee era, and Gao Yuheng, the Director of Industry, have both resigned. Zhao Pengdi has been appointed as the puppet Director of Finance, and Liang Yushu has been appointed as the puppet Director of Industry. The Municipal Affairs Office has been renamed the Municipal Affairs Department, expanding its powers to manage the municipal affairs of the entire city of Shenyang, with Zhao Xinbo still serving as the mayor. All of Zhao's concurrent positions have not been changed to reward his labor. Zhao is trusted by the Japanese, and Zang's rise to power this time was also orchestrated by him. (December 20th)

Guangzhou Students to Petition in Beijing

Resolved to Petition the Government on Seven Points

Guangzhou Dispatch: After the Guangzhou students held a large petition on the 17th of this month, they resolved on the same day to organize a national salvation petition group to prepare to go to Nanjing to carry out a large-scale petition. On that day, Xiang Hanping, the representative of the Guangdong government, promised that the Guangdong government would allocate travel expenses. Therefore, the students of the entire city have been preparing for days to elect representatives for the trip north and have agreed to elect three representatives from each school and request the Guangdong government to allocate 300 silver dollars in travel expenses per person, with the intention to set off north on the 21st.

At the same time, the following demands were resolved to be made to the Nanjing government: (A) Request the government to allow the Guangdong army to pass through and recover the lost territories in the Northeast. (B) Request the government to simultaneously send troops to recover the lost territories. (C) Request the government to dismiss and investigate Zhang Xueliang, who neglected his duty in defending the territory, and permanently deprive him of his civil rights. (D) Request the government to dismiss and investigate the military police who shot students participating in patriotic movements, and allow absolute freedom for patriotic movements in the future. (E) Request the government to make diplomacy and finance absolutely transparent. (F) Request the government not to directly negotiate with Japan before Japan withdraws its troops. (G) The Guangzhou Student Anti-Japanese Movement Joint Association requests the Guangdong government to guarantee in writing that the Guangdong army will send troops solely to recover the lost territories and will not have other uses. After the above proposals were agreed upon, each school has been separately selecting representatives for days, with a total of more than two hundred representatives being elected. They immediately requested the Guangdong government to fulfill its promise and issue more than 70,000 yuan in travel expenses. However, because the Guangdong government considered this amount of travel expenses to be too large, it must be submitted for discussion and approval at the State Council meeting on the 22nd before it can be issued. Therefore, the date for the representatives to go north to petition has been delayed. Once the travel expenses are received, the student delegation can depart. In addition, the student community recently requested the Guangdong government to quickly send personnel to train student volunteer soldiers. When the Student Anti-Japanese United Association was established, a military training committee was organized. Recently, the Guangdong government also established a student army training committee. Yesterday, student representatives asked Xiang Hanping, the representative of the Guangdong government, to explain how the powers of these two committees are defined. Xiang said that military training is a matter of military secrets, and of course, the military training committee organized by the national government is the formal guiding agency, and the military training committee organized by the Student Association can only serve as a liaison agency. Afterwards, the student representatives requested instructions on the allocation methods, which should be based on schools, with fifty people per class, and two hours of training per day. The allocation of instructors has also become a problem. Because He Tong, the General Supervisor of Student Military Training, is still in Hong Kong and has not indicated whether he will take office, at least three hundred instructors are needed to handle the training. The government intends to have graduates from the Whampoa Military Academy or students from the First Army Corps Academy serve as instructors, but it has not yet been decided. (December 22nd)

Missing Leader of the Mongolian Youth Party

According to Japanese sources, Gotengfu Wang, the leader of the Mongolian Youth Party, has recently disappeared suddenly. It is reported that Gotengfu Wang was in Hailar earlier this month and then went to Manzhouli. His concubine is currently traveling in Russia. Wang went to the Soviet consulate a few days ago to request a passport and has not been seen since. It is rumored that he has been kidnapped by suspicious Soviet merchants. It is also rumored that Wang intended to take advantage of the situation and lead Mongolian soldiers to launch an uprising in southern Manchuria, so he was assassinated by the Mongolian Communist Party's Dai Luolishi De.

Part of Japan's Illegal Pending Cases (7)

Fuzhou Japanese Consulate Arbitrarily Removes Seals on Opium Den Case: The Yifa Foreign Firm's opium den at No. 5 Gaojie Lane, Fuzhou City, was previously declared by the Japanese Consul stationed in Fuzhou as having no connection with Japanese nationals. On August 15th of the 19th year [of the Republic], the opium den was raided by the authorities, and the case was transferred to the court for investigation, and the building was sealed. The Japanese Consul suddenly claimed that although the Yifa Foreign Firm had been declared to have no connection with Japanese nationals, Consul had permitted Japanese national, Hou Yi's request to operate in the house selling marine products. They requested the seal be removed to allow Hou Yi to reside there temporarily for one and a half months. While negotiations were underway, on October 23rd, the Japanese Consul suddenly sent personnel to destroy the seal on the building. Japanese national Hou Yi then re-displayed scattered sundry goods in the building. Furthermore, in March of the 20th year [of the Republic], the Japanese Consul stationed in Fuzhou privately removed the seal on the opium den at No. 2 Houtian Lane, which had been sealed by order, and affixed a seal of the Japanese Imperial Consulate in Fuzhou. The opium den was also owned by Japanese national Lin Luogu. Based on the facts, we successively sent documents to the Japanese Ambassador to China for negotiations, but received no response.

Conflict Between Chinese and Japanese Military Police in Longjing Village: Around 9 PM on October 6th of the 19th year [of the Republic], while Longjing Village, Yanji, was under curfew, more than ten armed individuals advanced towards the army post on Xin'an Street. Upon being questioned, they suddenly opened fire. The sentries returned fire. It was later discovered that two were killed and one was injured, all of whom were Japanese police officers. Using this as a pretext, Japan dispatched a large number of armed police officers, who entered the country freely. We immediately sent a letter to the Japanese Chargé d'Affaires in China, requesting him to urgently telegraph the Japanese government, ordering the Japanese police officers who had arrived in Longjing to be immediately withdrawn. At the same time, we telegraphed the Northeast Political Affairs Committee to investigate the truth and negotiate a resolution with the Japanese Consul nearby. On November 20th, the Northeast Political Affairs Committee telegraphed back, stating that the case had been resolved through negotiations between the Director of the Yanji Municipal Preparatory Office and the Japanese Consul-General. The resolution included: (1) The Director expressed regret to the Consul-General; (2) Those responsible and those who acted would be punished, and an oral notification would be given; (3) A condolence payment of 10,000 Japanese yen and medical expenses of 200 yen would be paid within one week. It is currently unknown whether the case has been closed, as no reports have been received from the local authorities.

Japanese Military Oppression of the Andong City Electric Light Plant Case: On April 28th of this year, the Andong City Electric Light Plant sent workers to the north of the Ba Dao Gou Railway to replace wooden poles. While they were working, Japanese railway guards spotted them and suddenly brought dozens of guards, who watched over the workers and took away the construction ropes. The plant manager, upon hearing the news, immediately went with the secretary of the county government to reason with them and explain the situation. By this time, the number of guards who had arrived had reached five to six hundred, armed with live ammunition, intimidating them in every possible way, and forcing the county government secretary to issue a written apology on the spot. The captain of the guards, Heng You, was particularly egregious. Only after they had fully indulged in their violence did they release the workers.

Japanese Warships "Fuyo" and Others Sail into Inland Rivers Case: At 3 PM on May 18th of this year, the Japanese cruiser "Fuyo" sailed from the Guanhai River estuary, passing through Shuanggang, directly into Xiangshui Estuary, taking photographs along the way, and anchoring for about ten minutes. Later, due to the large number of onlookers, the ship lowered its Japanese flag and set sail out of the estuary. Based on dispatches from the Jiangsu Provincial Government and the Ministry of Finance, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs sent a note to the Japanese Chargé d'Affaires in China on June 20th, stating that the Japanese warship had entered Chinese inland rivers without the permission of our government and had taken photographs along the way, which violated international practice and disregarded Chinese sovereignty. It sternly ordered the Japanese warship not to enter Chinese territory without permission in the future. According to the Japanese reply on July 9th, the Japanese warship "Fuyo" did take photographs along the Guanhai River to Xiangshui, but this was done according to the usual peaceful practices and did not have any hostile intent. Furthermore, the photography was done outside the fortress area and was merely for sightseeing, and did not violate international practice or infringe on sovereignty. We again sent a note to the Japanese side on July 21st, stating that foreign warships must not enter without notifying the government of the host nation, which is an international practice recognized by all countries. We again requested that they strictly instruct their warships to comply. However, the Japanese side replied again on August 18th, stating that foreign warships can enter any port in China under the treaty, and there is no doubt about the above principle based on past practice. We also received a telegram from the Hunan Provincial Government stating that the Japanese gunboat "Toba" had sailed to Xiangtan, and we protested to the Japanese side on September 5th together in a single case. Regarding the statement that foreign warships can enter any port in China under the treaty, there is no such provision in the Sino-Japanese Commercial Treaty, which has already expired. The Japanese side replied again on September 16th, stating that foreign warships can enter any port in China under the treaty, and Japanese warships can enjoy the same treatment based on the most-favored-nation clause. There is no doubt about the understanding between China and Japan regarding maintaining the current state of the Sino-Japanese Commercial Treaty and treaty relations.

Japanese Military Forcibly Occupies Farmland in Linyu as a Firing Range Case: Four residents of Linyu County, Hebei, Wang Ziliang, Chi Chengjiu, Zhao Jingxu, and Chu Chengming, owned land located north of Tujiazhuang in the 16th township of the 1st district of the county, which was a little over two li away from the Japanese garrison camp. The garrison did not notify Wang Ziliang and his tenants, forcibly removed the crops from the fields, and occupied them as a firing range. They also dug trenches about 400 bow in length and 50 bow in width on both sides as boundaries. When Wang and his tenants, as well as the village leaders of Tujiazhuang, tried to reason with them, the garrison was unreasonable and continued to occupy the land. In June of the 20th year [of the Republic], Wang and others filed a complaint with the Ministry of Foreign Affairs.

Second Korean Riot Case: On July 2nd of this year, Japanese and Korean newspapers, taking advantage of the Wanbaoshan Incident, issued special editions, fabricating facts and inciting Koreans to riot against the Chinese. Massacres of overseas Chinese occurred successively in Incheon, Gyeongseong, Pyongyang, Zhennampo, Wonsan, Sinuiju, and other places. Pyongyang was particularly severe, and the riots spread throughout Korea for more than ten days. A total of 143 overseas Chinese were killed, 72 were missing, 343 were injured, and direct losses were estimated at 3 million Japanese yen, with countless indirect losses. At that time, the Consul-General stationed in Korea negotiated for protection and suppression, but the other side was evasive and did not make serious preparations afterward, intentionally neglecting the case. After lodging a protest with the Japanese ambassador, the other side repeatedly used the Wanbaoshan incident as an excuse and refused to take responsibility. Later, an eight-point solution was proposed, including apology, punishment of the perpetrators, compensation for deaths and injuries, and guarantees of future security, but no reply has been received.

Japanese Police Use Protection as an Excuse: Korean Farmers from Wanbaoshan Arbitrarily Enter the Interior Case: Hao Yongde, manager of the Changchun Changnong Company, leased over 400 xiang of barren land in Wanbaoshan in April of this year and recruited Korean nationals to plant rice. The county approved an order for investigation, but did not approve the filing of the case (the lease stipulated that it would be invalid if the county government did not approve it). However, Hao immediately brought over 180 Korean nationals into the country, digging waterways more than 20 li long, occupying and destroying farmland, directly connecting to the riverbank, and intercepting the river to build dams. The people nearby, fearing that tens of thousands of mu of cultivated land on both sides would be destroyed, gathered representatives to request the county government and the Municipal Preparatory Office to stop it. The county sent police to suppress and disperse the Koreans. However, the Japanese Consul had already sent six police officers to the scene to interfere. Later, the Jilin Provincial Government and the Japanese Consul-General agreed to withdraw the police and discuss the matter further. After the police were withdrawn, the Changchun authorities agreed that the Koreans would stop work and that both sides would jointly investigate and make a decision. After the joint investigation, the Municipal Office drafted a solution and submitted it to the Japanese Consul. However, the Japanese Consul completely rejected the restoration of the destroyed farmland and the cessation of river dam construction. He also ordered a large group of Koreans and sent five or sixty plainclothes police officers, carrying machine guns, to forcibly occupy civilian houses, claiming to protect the work and the completion of the river dam project. On July 1st, three to four hundred people, each holding chisels and hoes, went to fill in the water intakes. The Japanese police suddenly opened fire on the people, and our police tried their best to suppress the situation to prevent a major incident. The Changchun Municipal Office protested on the basis of reason, but the Japanese side completely ignored it. The Jilin Provincial Government then telegraphed the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, and on July 22nd, a note was sent to the Japanese Ambassador stating that Wanbaoshan was not a residential area, and Korean farmers were not allowed to go there. The lease agreement between them and Hao Yongde had not been approved for filing. Local officials had the responsibility to maintain public order and protect foreigners, so how could the Japanese police arbitrarily enter the interior? They requested the Japanese Ambassador to transfer the order and quickly withdraw the Japanese police who had been sent. The contract between the Korean farmers and Hao Yongde would naturally not take effect. If there were losses due to the lease, they should be compensated. The Chinese farmers should also be compensated by the Korean farmers for the losses caused by digging waterways and other damages to the fields. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs' note was fair in its attitude and originally hoped for an early and impartial solution to avoid disputes. However, the Japanese Ambassador replied on August 26th that he did not pay attention to the fact that Hao Yongde had no right to enter into a contract with the Korean farmers, and the Korean farmers had no right to occupy the farmland in Wanbaoshan. Instead, he said that it was necessary for the Japanese Consul to send armed Japanese police to assist the illegal work of the Korean farmers. He believed that the Chinese police's legal dissolution of the Korean farmers who were illegally cultivating farmland, digging ditches, and building dams in Wanbaoshan was a policy of oppression, disregarding treaty law, reason, and facts. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs replied to the Japanese Ambassador on September 15th, the main points of which were: (1) This time, the Korean farmers' cultivation of farmland, digging ditches, and building dams involved criminal matters. Our police's obstruction was the proper exercise of administrative power and should not be considered oppression of Korean farmers. The Japanese note said that the Korean farmers' lease agreement with Hao had been approved by the county magistrate, and an understanding had been reached with the landowners of the waterway, so the waterway project began in mid-April, and local officials and related landowners never interfered, which was not the case. Moreover, the Korean farmers' lease agreement with Hao had not been approved by the county government. When the Korean farmers went to Sun Yongqing and other places in April, they were stopped and work was suspended by Sun Yongqing and Ma Baoshan and others. After that, work was suspended and resumed several times. How could there have been a prior understanding? (2) The Japanese note said that the Korean farmers' actions were all in good faith and that if floods occurred due to the water conservancy project, the Korean farmers were prepared to compensate. The original lease contract of Hao Yongde had not been approved by the county, so it was invalid from the beginning. Therefore, regardless of whether the Korean farmers' lease was in good faith, the contract between the Korean farmers and Hao Yongde could not produce any rights. The Korean farmers' cultivation of farmland, digging ditches, and building dams were all illegal. Moreover, the digging of ditches was outside the wasteland leased in the contract between them and Hao, which was even more illegal. The Korean farmers themselves knew that it was illegal, so they prepared to compensate for the losses, which could hardly avoid criminal responsibility. (3) According to the Tumen River Boundary Treaty, Korean people were only allowed to cultivate and reside in specific areas of Yanji, Helong, and Wangqing north of the Tumen River. Assuming that the land leased by the Korean farmers in this case was within the scope of that area, they still could not obtain any rights due to the invalidity of the contract. Moreover, this case was outside the area allowed by the treaty, and the contract they signed was invalid. Regarding the issue of the Sino-Japanese Treaty of 1915 mentioned in the Japanese note, that issue was originally a minor matter in this case under the above judgment. Moreover, a formal statement was made to the Japanese side in March 1923. (4) In short, the Chinese authorities are legally suppressing those who want to acquire rights illegally, and there is no intention to oppress Korean farmers. Based on the above reasons, Korean farmers cannot cultivate or occupy farmland in Wanbaoshan. Please transfer the order and order the Korean farmers to withdraw from the area immediately. The legal relationship between the Korean farmers and Hao Yongde arising from the invalid contract should be resolved as soon as possible. The losses of the Chinese farmers should still be compensated by the Korean farmers as soon as possible to resolve the matter. After the Ministry of Foreign Affairs issued this second note, the Japanese side has not yet replied.

Tumen River Japanese Military Exercise Case: In August of this year, the Northeast Political Affairs Committee telegraphed that the engineering unit in Hoe Ryong, Korea, planned to conduct bridge-building and marching exercises on the banks of the Yuchuan River for three weeks starting from the 4th of this month. Over 200 Japanese soldiers arrived in Chengchuan on the Japanese bank of the Tumen River. On the 8th, Japanese ships were seen on the Chinese bank, and the number of Japanese soldiers in Chengchuan increased by 400. Eight tents were set up, and 30 sailboats carrying over 100 Japanese soldiers sailed from Hoe Ryong to Chengchuan. By the 11th, 34 Japanese engineers had intruded into our country's riverbank, burying two wooden stakes and inserting small red and green flags for bridge building and surveying. The Magistrate of Unchun County repeatedly protested to the Japanese Consul there, Chang Er, and informed him to stop the bridge building. The Japanese Consul agreed to transfer the order, but said that the exercise was fixed and it would be difficult to stop. The Tumen River is a river shared by China and Japan. The Japanese military's bridge-building exercises in the basin violated international law and infringed on Chinese sovereignty. We sent a note to the Japanese ambassador on the 14th to stop it and prevent such actions from happening again. However, at 1 PM on the 15th, six or seven Japanese engineers set off 25 explosions in the center of the river. At 4 PM, 30 engineers rode in two small motorboats and toured in the center of the river for about nine hours. Over 30 Japanese guards, carrying two machine guns, crossed our riverbank to conduct exercises and fired three times. We still checked the note on the 14th and sent a second note to the Japanese ambassador on the 26th, strictly prohibiting it, but received no reply. Furthermore, according to a report from the Northeast Border Defense Army Headquarters, the commander of the Japanese 19th Division, Mori Hisashi, came to Hunchun on the morning of the 17th and left at 6 PM in the afternoon. At 4 PM that afternoon, Japanese engineers transported seven floating bridge piers using iron boats. On the 18th, they transported 12 more and a steamer sailed upstream. At 3 AM on the 19th, the bridge piers were transported back to Qingyuan Crossing, and over 200 Japanese soldiers built a bridge on our shore, fixing about five bridge piers and floating 35 bridge piers, completing it at 9 AM. About 100 infantrymen passed back and forth twice from the east bank. At 10 PM on the 18th, at Jiaxinzai on the eastern side of the boundary river, there were five Japanese soldiers, a searchlight, and over 100 Japanese soldiers on both the east and west banks of the river, each carrying two machine guns, conducting confrontation exercises. The Japanese soldiers on the west side boarded boats to cross the river, and the Japanese soldiers on the east side resisted, preventing the river from being crossed and shooting at each other. The exercise stopped at 3 PM on the 19th and completely withdrew, crossing over to the west bank. At 12 PM that day, the previously built pontoon bridge was dismantled, and over 100 vehicles were hired to transport all the materials used in the Tumen River exercise completely away. This exercise was completed on the 20th, and there were no traces of Japanese troops in the area on the 21st. (End)

Local Correspondence

Songjiang

Robbery Occurs in Busy Market: The west outside Songjiang City is the most prosperous commercial area. Unexpectedly, at 9:30 PM last night (the 25th), the door of the Fangsheng Rice Store, across from the County Chamber of Commerce in Mojia Lane, was already closed, and only the husband and wife were inside. Suddenly, three thugs arrived, one holding a handgun guarding the door, and the other stealing assaulted the shop owner and beat him severely, forcing him to hand over money. The shop owner's wife tried to escape and shout for help, but the thug with the gun fired three shots. The thugs escaped before they could search. Coincidentally, Water Patrol Officer Fei Gongxia was passing by and chased after them, capturing one thug named Cao Huisheng. The others escaped without a trace. Later, patrolling police officers Yu Ziqin and Li Shijie from the Fourth Precinct captured two of the escaped thugs, He Guxiang and Yang Qinjia, in an empty room east of the Mingxing Bridge station, along with a handgun. After preliminary interrogation by Officer Ma, He confessed to being a native of Suzhou and working as a tailor, and Yang confessed to being a local from the South Gate. They both confessed to the robberies at Lianqing Nunnery outside the South Gate and the small teahouse opened by Zhu Bingsheng earlier this month. They were immediately prepared to be sent to the County Public Security Bureau for investigation.

Jiading

Kidnapping of Township Chief Case Solved: Township Chief Lu Jinyu of Chaoan Township in the Fifth District of the county was kidnapped on the night of the 17th of this month and has been missing since. Unexpectedly, this morning, judicial police officer Wang Songlan and others were investigating a kidnapping case and went to the north gate to arrest matchmaker Gu Fusheng. During a search of his home, Lu Jinyu was unintentionally found, along with two kidnappers, Dong Laisheng and Gu Xuezhi, from Qingjiangpu, and a handgun. Gu Fusheng escaped and has not been captured. His father, Tingyi, along with the kidnapped victim and the kidnappers, were all sent to the county. Under close interrogation by Investigator Zhang, Gu Tingyi confessed that Lu and Gu were led to his home by his son Fusheng and Zhu Axi, who ran a butcher shop at Cheng Bridge outside the East Gate, at midnight on the 22nd. The county government immediately sent police to Cheng Bridge to arrest Zhu and detain him for questioning.

Suzhou

Details of Robbery at Qian Songyao's Home: At 5:30 PM on the 25th, seven robbers armed with weapons robbed the home of Qian Bingjun (Songyao), the elder brother of Qian Dajun, at No. 28 Sipo Lane, Suzhou City, causing losses of approximately 7,000 to 8,000 yuan. This was briefly reported in yesterday's newspaper. It is now known that Qian Songyao himself had gone to Ningbo and had not returned. Only his wife, maid, coachman, and five others were at home. Suddenly, seven robbers arrived, carrying two handguns, claiming to be delivering a letter. When the coachman, A'er (also known as Gengsheng), opened the door, the robbers rushed in, displayed their handguns, drove the servants to the kitchen, and guarded the telephone and doors. They went straight upstairs and robbed the house. Afterwards, the hostess inspected the lost items and found that they had been robbed of over 200 yuan in silver dollars, four diamond rings, one diamond bracelet, and gold jewelry and fine clothing worth approximately 7,000 to 8,000 yuan.

Learning Martial Arts Leads to Minor Homicide: The ten-year-old son of Dr. Jiang Xijiu, who lives in Xihai Islandkou, Chengtian Temple, and A'yuan, the fifteen-year-old son of his neighbor Chen Guanda, were practicing martial arts in Guangdi a week ago. Unexpectedly, Jiang's son accidentally stabbed Chen's son A'yuan in the neck with a spear, which was quite dangerous. He was sent to the Gospel Hospital for treatment, but on the afternoon of the 25th, Chen A'yuan died from his injuries. His father, Chen Guanda, reported to the authorities and requested that the murderer be arrested and brought to justice. Jiang Xijiu, fearing punishment, has fled with his son.

Wuxi

Provincial Order Urges Collection of Cotton Business Tax: The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Finance, based on a report from the Changshu County Chamber of Commerce, stated in a letter from Zhang Shouyi, the head of the Cotton Business Tax Collection Committee in Changshu County, that the county is a cotton-producing area. Every harvest season, yarn factories from neighboring counties send personnel to Changshu to set up cotton collection points, which all close by the end of autumn and the beginning of winter. This year, when the business tax was first collected, these cotton collection points were repeatedly urged to pay the tax. However, the collection points initially denied it and then procrastinated. For example, the Wuxi Guangqin Yarn Factory had a business volume of 270,000 yuan, and the short-term business tax should be 2 per mille, totaling 540 yuan. Qingfeng's business volume was 240,000 yuan, and the tax should be 488 yuan. Yukan's business volume was 280,000 yuan, and the tax should be 560 yuan. Shenxin's business volume was 220,000 yuan, and the tax should be 440 yuan. Zhenxin's business volume was 110,000 yuan, and the tax should be 220 yuan. After receiving the report, the department yesterday issued a special order to the county government of this city, immediately ordering the above factories to strictly collect and report. After receiving the order, County Magistrate Chen has already complied.

Daytime Robbery on Main Street in City: The Cheng Silver Shop on Main Street in the city, which was established with funds raised by Fang Youhe, has been doing well in business. At 3 PM yesterday (the 26th), a rogue wearing short clothes suddenly entered the shop under the pretext of exchanging gold rings. Shop assistant Feng Nianzu took out two gold rings and placed them on the counter. Unexpectedly, the rogue dared to take advantage of the unpreparedness of the people and robbed them, fleeing towards Xiangchengjiao. Seeing this, Feng Nianzu immediately stepped forward to chase and shout for the thief, and other shop assistants joined in the chase. The rogue was captured, and the patrolling police from the Fourth Precinct brought him into the station. Chief Zhu of the precinct held a preliminary trial. The suspect confessed his name was Li Da and admitted to robbing the Cheng Silver Shop of gold rings. After verifying the confession, Chief Zhu believed that the suspect dared to commit robbery in broad daylight in the busy market, which was extremely illegal. He immediately prepared a document to send to the General Bureau for investigation.

Chief of the 16th Precinct Bribed to Replace Smuggler: Shen Jizhou, Chief of the 16th Precinct of the Public Security Bureau in Anzhen, District 8 (Huai Xia City), has been in office for less than a month. On the afternoon of the 11th of this month, Bureau member Huang Bingjian led police officers Zhao Changchun and Wang Jinshan on patrol in the east market of the town when they discovered a drug offender named Cai Juquan, and found two bags of opium and three cans of red pills (totaling 318 pills) on him. He was immediately taken to the bureau. After Chief Shen held a preliminary trial, it is unknown how, he released the drug offender Cai Juquan and hired Mi Tiansheng, who was addicted to red pills, to go to the bureau, impersonating him. The next day, he was vaguely sent to the Public Security Bureau. When Section Chief Fu Hongsheng of the Third Section learned of this, he conducted a detailed study of the case with Section Member Zhang Shuping and realized that the precinct chief and bureau members had taken bribes to cover up evidence. He reported to Chief Hua and sent Inspector Zhang Zijing to the countryside to investigate and verify the facts, and obtained a written certificate signed jointly by Patrol Captain Yin Hongsheng and police officer Zhao Changchun of the precinct. He returned to the bureau and reported to Chief Hua for verification. Later, Section Chief Fu interrogated the arrested fake Cai Juquan. The suspect confessed that his name was Mi Tiansheng and he was replacing Cai Juquan in the case. Chief Fu verified the confession and immediately sent police to the countryside to summon the real Cai Juquan and Gu Dongliang to the case. Yesterday, along with Mi Tiansheng, they were all transferred to the County Court for trial. As for how the precinct chief and bureau members should be dealt with, Chief Hua will report to the county government for verification.

Jiangyin

Bandit Alarm Occurs in Shenzhuang Township: Shenzhuang Township along the river in Shengang is a place where pirates haunt. There had been robberies before. Around 8 PM on the 24th, eight or nine people in military uniforms, each with quick guns and sabers, were reported to the Fifth District Public Security Bureau Security Corps. They urgently telegraphed the Sixth District Corps Police to go and search for them. Seven people were arrested on the spot, all of whom were deserters from Liang Guanying's troops of the 25th Route Army in Jiangbei. It was scheduled to send to the city today (the 26th).

Director of Land Tax Detention for Overdue Payment: The County Government Finance Bureau was previously ordered by the Provincial Department to pay 70,000 yuan in advance of the winter grain tax to fund the Grand Canal labor debt. The two heads of the County Bureau once convened a meeting of various agencies, borrowing 30,000 yuan from various money houses and factories, and offsetting 40,000 yuan from the business owners, all to be returned to the money houses by the end of the lunar year this year. 40,000 yuan was paid on the 23rd, but it was not paid on time. County Magistrate Ma detained Chen Jingshan, the director of land tax, yesterday (the 24th) because he was not effective in raising funds, and ordered the Public Security Bureau to detain Chen. In the afternoon, an emergency meeting of various agencies was convened to discuss how to deal with the overdue payment of more than 200,000 land taxes. It was resolved to rectify the method and limit Chen to pay 40,000 yuan within a few days. At the same time, the reasons for the delayed payment were reported to the Provincial Department.

Nantong

Wuxue Ship Searches for Opium Soil Negotiations: British Vice-Consul Gittens stationed in Shanghai arrived in Tong on the afternoon of the 24th on the HMS Cricket to investigate the search for opium soil by the 25th Route Army stationed in Nantong's Yaogang on the Taikoo Company's Wuxue Ship. The British Vice-Consul also met with Shang Xihe, the head of the inspection office. Shang immediately told him the details of what happened. The British warship was still at Yaogang on the 25th. It is heard that the negotiations regarding the search for opium are now being handled by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs.

Guard Corps Changes to Conscription System: The Tongyi Guard Corps has been established in 18 districts, and in less than two years, more than 700,000 yuan has been spent. At present, it is difficult to raise these funds. The county government specially convened the district chiefs to discuss relief measures and decided to change to a conscription system in order to save public funds.

Zhenjiang

Two Public Bonds to be Drawn on Schedule: The repayment date for the third Jiangsu Provincial Construction Bond is January 31st, the 21st year of the Republic of China. The Department of Finance has now scheduled the public drawing to be held at 3:00 PM on January 11th at the Zhenjiang Chamber of Commerce. The drawing of the old Jiangsu Rehabilitation Bonds will also be conducted as an adjunct. In addition to requesting personnel from the Provincial Government to jointly handle the matter, reports will also be submitted to the Ministries of Finance and Audit, which will send personnel to supervise in due course to ensure prudence.

Student Commits Suicide Out of Grief for National Affairs: Zhu Shikui, a student at the Provincial Zhenjiang Middle School, was a native of Taixing and the son of Zhu Xingfu. He was known for his composure and outstanding talent, and was considered a promising individual by the local gentry. Recently, Zhu became indignant at the violent invasion by Japan, fearing the nation would perish. He intended to rally his comrades to join the volunteer army and fight the Japanese invaders to the death. Someone informed his father of this by letter. His father, a merchant, was ignorant of national affairs and deeply loved his son. He tricked his son into returning home with a telegram on other matters. Upon learning he had been deceived, Zhu became despondent. He wrote two letters to his classmates, expressing guilt for not being able to face the national crisis with them and hoping that his classmates would strive to kill the enemy. On the 20th, he ingested four mace of opium. The dose was lethal, and he could not be saved. He died shortly thereafter at the young age of eighteen. His father was overwhelmed with grief and deeply regretted his actions after his death.

Huzhou

Military and Bandits Exchange Fire at Yangjia Kiln: Company Commander Zheng of the Third Company, First Battalion, Seventh Regiment of the city's Security Brigade, was ordered some time ago to proceed to the western countryside to suppress bandits. On the 21st, he learned that a large number of bandits were holding a captive for ransom in the Yangjia Kiln area near Lijia Lane. The company commander immediately led a platoon of soldiers to the foot of the mountain about half a mile from Yangjia Kiln, where they encountered the bandits. The two sides exchanged fire for about half an hour. The bandits were unable to withstand the attack and fled in all directions. Several bandits were killed on the spot, and one Mauser pistol was seized. Guo Wenzhong, the captive, was rescued. It is now known that the regimental headquarters has ordered Company Commander Zheng to send the captive back to the regimental headquarters to await his family's claim.

Ningbo

Eighteen-Year-Old Nun Kidnapped: Yesterday, more than ten bandits suddenly arrived at the Yongfeng Nunnery near Yingjiang Bridge in western Yin County, surrounded the temple, and searched for valuables. Finding nothing, they kidnapped an eighteen-year-old nun from the temple and demanded a ransom of five hundred yuan.

Anqing

Provincial Government Replaces Four County Magistrates: At the 229th regular meeting held on the 22nd, the Anhui Provincial Government resolved to replace the magistrates of Wuyuan, Yi, Wuwei, and She counties, as well as the director of the provincial capital's Public Security Bureau, as follows: Qi Qingchi, the magistrate of Wuyuan County, was removed from his post, and Ke Kaiyun was appointed to act in his stead. Zhang Songjiu, the magistrate of Yi County, had not yet taken office and should be replaced. Gao Chongyou, the magistrate of Wuwei County, was transferred to act in his stead, leaving the post of Wuwei County vacant, which was filled by Gao Shouheng acting in his stead. Miao Dingbao, the magistrate of She County, was transferred to the province, and Hu Zhaogong was appointed to act in his stead. Li Yue, the director of the provincial capital's Public Security Bureau, resigned, and Ding Handong was appointed to succeed him. Furthermore, Yang Guanying, the magistrate of Huoqiu County, encountered danger while on official duty and was granted a compensation of one thousand yuan.

Page 10

Important Educational News

Educational Circles of Songjiang County

Request Rectification of Primary School Education

The colleagues of the educational circles of Songjiang County, Jiangsu Province, sent an express telegram which reads: Urgent. Via Shenbao, to the members of the Fourth Plenary Session of the First Central Executive Committee, including committee member Mr. Hengyuan, and all committee members, for your review. Education is the foundation of a nation, and culture is the light of a people. If we want the country to prosper and the nation to unite, we must rely on education, especially primary school education. Everyone knows this. Consider Japan's Meiji Restoration, which prioritized primary school education. In just a few decades, the results were remarkable. Since the beginning of the Republic of China, the rulers have not failed to emphasize primary school education. However, most of the national funding is used for military expenditures, leaving no specific funds to subsidize education in local areas. In some cases, provincial authorities have even issued orders to cut schools or reduce school funding and teacher salaries due to local financial constraints. Looking at this county, in recent years, even without a shortage of educational funding, there have still been cases of cutting schools, reducing school funding, and lowering teacher salaries. This is true even without the excuse of financial difficulties in other counties. In this era, even if we cannot expand education rapidly, we should at least ensure that educators are not burdened by the pressures of life and can teach with peace of mind, thereby increasing the efficiency of teaching. If China wants to promote national spirit and revitalize the country, it must rely on primary school education. The quality of primary school education depends on primary school teachers. This goes without saying. The only way to achieve national survival under the oppression of the great powers is to rectify primary school education. Methods for rectifying primary school education: (1) The government should allocate specific funds to subsidize local primary school funding. (2) Expand primary school funding. (3) Increase primary school teacher salaries. If the above three points can be realized immediately, there is hope for China's future. We offer these humble suggestions and hope that they will be adopted. In haste and with utmost urgency. Colleagues in the educational circles of Songjiang County, Jiangsu Province, Qian Zingshou and 37 others, respectfully kowtow. [End]

Local News

Representatives' Meeting of Anti-Japanese Associations of Various Universities

Resolutions on the Tragedy and Domestic and Foreign Affairs

Request the Government to Respond in Writing to All Demands

The United Association of Anti-Japanese and National Salvation Students of various universities in this city held the 30th emergency meeting of representatives at the Jiangwan Road Law School at 10:00 AM yesterday (26th). The meeting was held to discuss whether they were satisfied with the results of the petition to the central government in Beijing by the delegation sent by their association. A representative of Jiangnan College who had returned from Beijing reported on the petition. Liu Chuanzhong of the Law School served as chairman, and Zhu Zushun served as the recorder.

Reports from All Parties: (1) Daxia reported that they had already notified the delegation in Beijing by long-distance telephone to proceed with the resolutions of the meeting of the executive committee of this association. (2) Representatives of the Nanjing delegation who had returned to Shanghai reported on their experiences in Beijing and their past and future work. (3) A representative of the Law School reported on the reception of journalists. After the reports, they immediately proceeded to

Discuss Key Matters: (1) Whether the Nanjing government is satisfied with the association's various demands: Resolved to discuss each item separately. (A) Regarding the tragedy: (1) Releasing arrested students: Request the government to immediately release the students who are still in custody. (2) Punishing instigators and murderers: Request the government to remove the Capital Garrison Commander and the Chief of Police. (3) Request the government to apologize to the people: Request the Garrison Headquarters to acknowledge that the deceased students were shot and killed by the military police. (4) Compensating the dead and wounded: Request the government to confirm the number requested by the association and immediately allocate funds for injury, burial, and medical expenses. (5) Retrieving the coffins: Considered satisfactory. (6) Guaranteeing that similar incidents will not occur again: Stated that the government denied prohibiting demonstrations. (B) Regarding domestic affairs: (1) Request the government to resolve and implement the points to which it has agreed to immediately. (2) Request the government to strictly stipulate that party members and those with notorious records shall not serve as national representatives. (3) Request the government to strictly order the execution of all those who undermine popular movements. (4) Omitted. (C) Regarding foreign affairs: (2) Regarding the National Salvation Conference: Resolved to request the new government to convene it immediately after its establishment. (3) Regarding military and financial affairs: Resolved to request the government to immediately concentrate national military force for war against Japan. (4) Regarding the disputes at yesterday's Fourth Plenary Session of the First Central Executive Committee: Resolved to request the committee members to put aside their prejudices and warn Wu Zhihui, Sun Ke, etc. (5) Regarding the numerous empty posts of ambassadors stationed abroad: Resolved to request the government to immediately order the ambassadors to take up their posts. (6) The first meeting of the joint association of university faculty and staff did not discuss the Northeast Incident, but instead held a singing performance to boost their refined spirits. How should we deal with this outrageous act? Resolved that the association considers it heartbreaking and issues a serious warning. (7) Regarding the Chen Deheng Ninth of September student unrest case, which concerns the reputation of all students in Shanghai, how should we deal with it? Resolved that Chen Deheng is merely a worker, how could he have such a large sum of money to place an advertisement? Furthermore, since many statements do not conform to the association's statements, it declares a refutation and orders the temporary court handling the Wang case to arrest and interrogate him. (8) What form should the government use to respond to the demands? Resolved to request the government to respond in writing. (9) During this national crisis, all sectors of society should stop New Year's greetings to express mourning. Resolved to pass and send a circular to all sectors of society to implement it. (10) Increasing membership fees: Resolved to temporarily increase by one yuan per hundred people based on the number of people. (11) The 31st meeting of representatives will be held next Monday (28th) at 1:00 PM at the Jin Shenfu Road School of Law and Politics. As for the issue of the remains of the deceased students that have not yet been transported back, due to time constraints, it will be moved to the next meeting of representatives for discussion.

Various Middle Schools

Students Yesterday Mourned the Deceased Students

More than 1,500 People Attended

The Atmosphere at the Venue was Solemn and Orderly

The United Association of Anti-Japanese and National Salvation Students of various secondary schools in this city held a memorial service for the deceased students who were killed during the demonstration in Beijing at the Jingye Middle School in Jukui Street, Xiaodongmen, at 10:00 AM yesterday. More than 1,500 students and guests from various schools attended. The atmosphere at the venue was extremely solemn, and the order was also very orderly. The details of the meeting are recorded below by a reporter from the Shanghai News Agency.

The Meeting: The bell rang ten times, announcing the start of the meeting. The ritual of paying respects was performed. The presidium, composed of Li Bin (Huizhen), Huang Shiti (Shanghai Middle School), and Chen Yubai (Wuben), reported on the significance of the meeting: A. Remembering the deceased students. B. Having a deeper understanding of the revolutionary government. C. Continuing the spirit of the deceased students and working twice as hard. Cai Ruoxian, a representative from Shanghai Middle School, reported on the situation of the tragedy at the time. Afterwards, they paid the highest respects to the spirits of the deceased students who were killed during the demonstration in Beijing with three bows and observed three minutes of silence for the deceased students. Then, Chen Yubai of Wuben presented a wreath, and Sun Yucai of Jingtang read the eulogy.

Full Text of the Eulogy: On December 26th of the 20th year of the Republic of China, all the students of Shanghai's middle schools offer this sacrifice to the spirits of the deceased students who were killed during the demonstration in Beijing, saying: Alas! The Japanese invaders are provoking incidents and occupying our Binyang, devouring and encroaching on our border regions like wolves and silkworms. Their greed is insatiable, and their military force is growing. Their ambition is to sweep across and engulf everything. If we do not resist them promptly, China will perish. The affairs of the nation have come to this, but why is it not good? The students, with great enthusiasm, are running around to help each other, fighting for the country and negotiating with the central government. However, their cotton gowns are mixed with weapons, and suddenly the soldiers raise their arms. In an instant, the blades are revealed, and their forms are suddenly exposed. They are forced to resist the enemy, and their skin and blood are scattered on the battlefield. Men die, but their loyalty shines brightly. Whose hands are responsible for this bloodshed? Looking upon your heroic spirits, we pour a cup of wine. Alas, may you be satisfied!

Speeches by Representatives: Attorney Wu Mailu, a member of the Executive Committee of the Municipal Anti-Japanese Association; Da Yijin, of the Propaganda Department of the Municipal Anti-Japanese Association; Qu Yicheng of Shanghai Middle School; Xiao Sizhi of Pudong Middle School; Zhang Shengpei and Wang Linxi of Junyi Middle School; Mao Yingyu of Patriotic Girls' Middle School; and Wang Weiyi of Municipal North Middle School delivered speeches in succession, expressing their condolences to the deceased students and elaborating on the issue of resisting Japan and saving the country. Their words were all filled with grief and indignation, moving the listeners. The meeting was adjourned after a group photo was taken at 1:00 PM in the afternoon. It was also heard that the association will hold its 13th meeting of representatives at Jingye Middle School in Jukui Street, Xiaodongmen, at 9:00 AM this morning.

Shanghai University Professors' Association

Upholding Academic Freedom...Urging the Release of Educational Funds

The Shanghai University Professors' Association was previously initiated by more than 80 people, including Zhou Junshi, Pan Guangdan, Dong Renjian, Li Guochang, Wu Zelin, Zhang Yisun, Han Bing, Lu Jizeng, Zhang Xiangshi, Zhang Zhifu, Quan Zenghu, Shen Youqian, Yu Nanqiu, and Wu Songgao, and has been in existence for nearly two years. Since the invasion by the Japanese invaders, it has contacted comrades to resist Japan and save the country, sparing no effort. Recently, in view of the rapidly changing situation and the many problems faced by universities, it has sent standing committee members to various places in Beijing and Ping to strive for academic freedom and urge the release of educational funds. It has also telegraphed universities across the country, requesting them to elect professor representatives to gather in Shanghai to discuss various issues such as upholding academic freedom, promoting higher education, and improving service and treatment.

Tough Meets Tough, No Clear Winner

Donghua and Western Police

| Result: 2 to 2 |

Chen Jiaqiu of Donghua, Wei Jinsheng of Western Police

| Amazing Performance |

By chance, Donghua took the lead 2-1 due to a re-taken penalty kick, and it seemed the victory would belong to Donghua today. However, in the blink of an eye, the match ended in a 2-2 draw. The more than ten thousand spectators at Yiyuan could not help but feel somewhat disappointed amidst their satisfaction. Looking at it from the other side, if Western Police had not lost a goal due to the penalty kick, they would have won 2-1. In short, the god of fortune did not want to favor one side, so the match ended in a 2-2 draw. Referee: Li Nuosi.

Xu Tu Huishe

Jipson Okelei

A Powerful Kick Breaks the Enemy's Net

At the start, the offensive went back and forth, with mutual opportunities. After ten minutes, Okelei heavily pressed the attack, and Huishe stepped forward to meet him. Center-back Tu Kaiyuan blocked him and passed it to right winger Chen Jiaqiu, who quickly advanced and kicked it towards the goal. Dai Linjing was prepared and took the opportunity to attack. The goalkeeper gained and lost control, and with a resounding sound, the enemy's net was breached.

Heading the Ball into the Goal Under Great Pressure

Afterwards, Western Police took advantage of the wind and became very aggressive. Left and right corner kicks were taken in turn. If it were not for Wei's strong resistance, the defense would have been breached. Falansi's shot towards the goal was fortunately blocked, otherwise it would have been disastrous. After forty minutes, Wei Jinsheng was active on the right flank and kicked a ball, which Falansi headed into the goal. The first half ended with each side scoring one goal.

Retaking the Penalty Kick Scores

After a short break, the teams reorganized and continued the match. Donghua's goalkeeper Zhou escaped death twice, showing his skills. Chen Hongguang dribbled the ball forward and suddenly fell. Zhu Na kicked him instead of the ball, resulting in a penalty kick. Dai kicked it in, but the referee ruled that Western Police players had entered the area before the kick and ordered it to be retaken. This time, Dai aimed accurately and kicked it in, taking the lead 2-1.

Wei Jinsheng Creates a Draw

Chen Jiaqiu made several wonderful crosses, creating a tense situation. The Western Police defenders did their best, but could not advance. At the critical moment, Donghua suddenly faced an emergency. Wei Jinsheng broke through the crowd and invaded, and by chance, kicked the ball into the net, creating a 2-2 draw.

Free Talk

Recollections of a Luxurious Home

— Yanzi

Yuan Shikai of the Hongxian era was indeed a hero of his time. However, he was misled by the encouragement of the "Six Gentlemen" and resolutely defied public anger, harboring the ambition to become emperor. Yet, he knew that without the support of imperialist powers, it would be ineffective. Zhou Ziqi's mission to Japan, even with lavish gifts, was rejected. Some say the Twenty-One Demands originated from this. At the beginning of Yuan Shikai's self-proclaimed emperorship, a sandalwood throne inlaid with nine dragons and huge pearls, costing over a million, was commissioned. The palace's round tables, cushioned pit chairs, and chair covers were all custom-made from Qiu Chen's satin shop with five-clawed nine-dragon round flower patterns, for which a deposit of 10,000 yuan was paid. They were working day and night to rush the order. By the time the work was completed, Yuan Shikai's imperial system had already melted away like ice and snow. As a result, the satin shop closed down. It is said that the losses amounted to 50,000 gold. This incident was known to the Japanese, who were willing to buy it back at a high price to keep it in a museum as a blemish. The owner of the satin shop refused. The Japanese returned in disappointment. Recently, it was heard that the five-clawed nine-dragon round table chair covers were sold to the Ministry of Railways for 30,000 gold. The dignified and magnificent brocade was not obtained by the Japanese invaders after all, which is somewhat gratifying.

Talks by a Humble Scholar from the Buchu Tingcao Studio

What I fear is a modern miss."

Our affection is like fish and water.
